申報 Amateur Weekly

Amateur Chats

What Kind of Elections Do We Need? 287

— Li Qiu

In recent weeks, Mr. Gongpu has repeatedly raised the issue of improving elections in this publication. Naturally, this issue is not only of significant importance in promoting municipal or local autonomy in practical terms, but also a crucial problem to be solved in the overall political transformation of China.

Although many past elections in China have failed due to unsound conditions, this should not be blamed on "elections" themselves. Because elections are only a method, and when people want the final judgment of social affairs to be in the hands of the majority, there is fundamentally no other method besides elections.

Therefore, our current demands for local autonomy and improved elections are actually to save and develop the spirit of democracy. We believe this is the minimum work to save the nation from political transformation and crisis.

Therefore, the current question is not whether we need to improve elections, but mainly what kind of elections we need. Regarding this, I believe:

First, what we need is universal suffrage. The gradual expansion of suffrage in modern times has progressed from class elections to universal elections. Therefore, we demand the abolition of all restrictions based on religion, economy, society, and gender. Everyone, except for underage children, patients with mental illness, and those deprived of their civil rights, should have the obligation and the right to participate in elections.

Second, we demand the expansion of real electoral power. The value of suffrage is mainly reflected in the number of elected officials. People's participation in elections is not only to elect advisory bodies for the government, but more importantly, to elect people who can represent their opinions and directly participate in the thorough resolution and execution of all major national or local issues. Therefore, we demand that the real power of elections should be expanded, and at the same time, we must save the implementation of the rights of initiative, referendum, and recall, because these three are interrelated.

Third, attention to election methods. We know that the value and effectiveness of suffrage are greatly related to voting methods. Open elections cannot fully express the will of the voters, and the "designated" election method completely loses the meaning of elections. Now, the election systems of various countries have almost all been changed to secret ballot systems. Therefore, we also demand that this election method be implemented in all elections in China.

Fourth, compulsory elections should be implemented. Suffrage is not only a right of the people but also a duty. Elections are a public service, and the state must use every means to ensure that the people perform this duty. In the past, the majority of our people were often indifferent to elections, on the one hand being manipulated by local tyrants and ambitious politicians, and on the other hand making the people uninterested in politics. Therefore, we advocate that the government should follow the example of countries such as Belgium, the Netherlands, the Czech Republic, and Spain, and implement a compulsory election system, stipulating that those who do not participate in elections should be subject to certain economic or reputational penalties.

Fifth, demand strict laws against election fraud. Election fraud was a common phenomenon in our country's past. Now, if we don't talk about elections, then so be it. Once we talk about elections, on the positive side, we demand raising the political awareness of the general public; on the negative side, we demand a strict law against election fraud. The state must use laws to stipulate that anyone who bribes, entertains, intimidates, impersonates, or illegally uses election funds or campaign workers must be given strict punishment.

The above are our minimum demands for improving elections. Some say that this is just an unattainable high-sounding ideal. In fact, we know that if an election can truly represent public opinion, and if the result of an election can gain the support of the majority of the people, what better method do we have other than elections based on the above points? Therefore, we hope that the authorities in charge of elections should take this as a goal to promote the implementation of sound elections. Whether it is central politics, local autonomy, or social organizations, if there cannot be perfect and sound elections, then all ideals cannot be achieved.

Indeed, "having elections is better than having no elections," but simply "having elections" is not enough. We must also demand more perfect elections within "having elections"!

Life

Blood Rice 288

— Long Lai

Living in this unreasonable society of "red doors reek of wine and meat, corpses lie frozen on the road," most people cannot even smell wine and meat. Rolling around on the line of hunger and death, in order to live, some have no choice but to painfully and cheaply auction off their labor, and some even sell their own children at low prices, stubbornly using the blood from their own bodies to exchange for leftovers to fill their bellies. This is what I want to talk about here: the working women who are hired by noble people to be wet nurses.

Just by walking through the "Employment Agencies" in Beijing, the "Matchmaking Shops" in Shanghai, or the "Human Markets" in Chengdu, and the "Guild Halls" in Chongqing, we will see these "blood sellers" squatting and sitting in rows like exhibits, waiting to be sold. Their eyes, filled with the bitter tears of separation from their husbands and children, are hungrily and attentively fixed on passersby. When they finally see a customer come in, they eagerly, for fear of making a mistake, hold out their eggplant-like breasts straight for people to choose and examine, feeling them up. As a result, those who are chosen leave with mixed feelings of sorrow and joy, following their masters (mostly to undergo blood tests by doctors). Those who are left behind after being picked over hang their heads in disappointment and wait for another customer. Who can see all this without feeling that it is a tragic drama? Aren't "blood sellers" even more pitiful than ordinary laborers?

Naturally, to give one's own blood to the sons and daughters of the nobles to suck, one must first put one's own children aside: the better option is to spend some money to entrust them to someone else's house, or leave them at home to be fed rice water; otherwise, if there is no one to entrust them to or no one to take care of them, one has no choice but to bear the pain and simply give them away or abandon them on the roadside or in the alley. When a person who does this kind of wet nursing holds someone else's child and feeds them her own milk, how deeply must she feel the pain in her heart! Especially when she sees the other person's child smiling at her with its little mouth open, reaching out its little hands to beckon her endearingly.

In terms of responsibility and work, wet nurses and ordinary maids and older sisters seem to be no different on the surface, but in reality, they are much more arduous than maids and older sisters. They not only bear the responsibility of feeding the child, but also have to bear the heavy responsibility for the child's development, health, illness, hygiene, etc. Therefore, once they are hired, they completely lose their freedom in terms of body and action. I remember there was such a tragicomedy: in the mansion of a couple who both claimed to be educators, the mistress supervised the wet nurse every day to rub some vanishing cream and face powder on her old melon-rind-like face, saying that her face was too ugly, and the girl would be afraid of resembling her in the future if she drank her milk. As a result, her face, which had been roughened by the wind and frost and haggard from labor, became feverish and painful from the cream and powder, so she couldn't tell whether to cry or laugh when she looked in the mirror. Speaking of action, it is simply no different from a prisoner in jail, because the young master or miss cannot go half a day or a night without feeding, so they are always unable to go home for a year or two. Clearly, they are married women, but the masters insist on them keeping "live widowhood." Not only that, but even walking around in the street or in a neighbor's house is subject to interference. If the child accidentally catches a cold and sneezes, then the masters will scold her for walking around with the child and catching a cold, and more severe masters will even use "deducting wages" and "getting out" to suppress her.

Washing the child's clothes and diapers, playing with the child, feeding milk, and rocking the cradle day and night, this is the general work of a wet nurse. In addition, buying vegetables, cooking,

Page 20

and doing needlework also have to be done. If the child is a little older, gradually grows teeth, and the sleep time is reduced, when they can barely crawl, then the wet nurse's work is no longer easy, and she must be careful to prevent him from falling at all times, and she must not leave her post even when sleeping. At this time, the child's every move is not as regular as when he was first born. Take his feeding as an example, before he is about to grow his small teeth, he will bite his nipples tightly while rubbing his gums, and after he has grown them, he will use his melon-seed-sized new teeth to tear and bite the nipples, often causing the wet nurse's face to twitch, but she cannot complain, and can only swallow the sour tears into her stomach. People eat people, this is really!

When the child is eight or nine months old, his appetite also increases compared to before. The wet nurse is always humbly afraid that her milk cannot satisfy him, and at the same time, she must diligently show the master that her milk is good, for fear that something will go wrong with her job. Therefore, whether it is day or night, as long as the child cries, she immediately puts her breasts into his mouth, letting that blood-sucking baby slowly suck, even if sometimes he sucks and hurts her flesh, emptying her blood, she has to endure the pain.

The leftovers in the messy cups and plates are the only food that the master gives to the wet nurse, and what they wear are the old, moldy clothes and pants from the bottom of their trunks. As for their wages, the highest is no more than ten yuan, and six or eight yuan is the most popular current price. If their own children are still being raised by someone else, then, in addition to the cost of raising their own children, what they earn besides the leftovers is only a thin body of anemia. This is the price of a "blood seller," this is the life of a blood-rice eater.

Chinese Language Teacher 289

— Wen Yu

People all know that Chinese language teachers are the most hardworking kind of teachers, but what kind of exhausting picture is actually unfolded in their lives is something that people may not fully understand. In the past year, I had the honor of being such a teacher in a private middle school in this city. I can't say that I really have much experience, but I don't deny that I do have some observations.

First of all, what I need to point out is the incorrect perception of these teachers in society. They think that education is noble, and therefore think that teachers, especially Chinese language teachers, are noble hermits who have not been stained by any earthly matters. But the fact is absolutely the opposite. Not only are they not noble hermits, not only do they need bread like ordinary people, but they also have to engage in fierce struggles for survival for bread. In this era of oversupply of talent, in order to hold on to their jobs, they have to use all kinds of methods to guard against competitors. Even if they want to be noble, they cannot.

Now I will show you the dark side of their lives here. Regardless of health, regardless of ability, they often teach at two, three, or even four or more schools. Some of them teach as many as five or six classes. In terms of hours, some of them teach thirty-six hours per week. They are completely using their bodies as machines. There is almost no talk of teaching efficiency here; we only see a group of people who are just trying to get by wriggling in the struggle.

The reason for this is obviously the excessive meager treatment, coupled with arrears in wages, so that what they earn each month with hard work may not even be enough to support their families. In this situation, what good way is there to call on them to pay attention to teaching efficiency and take on fewer hours?

According to the general situation of the education circle in China today, the price of their hard work is calculated by the hour, depending on the nature of the public or private school and the degree of development of that school, rather than the amount of their compensation. There is such a situation in Shanghai today: it is very difficult for teachers to receive their salaries at a middle school with only one or two years of history and about one hundred students, although the letter of appointment may stipulate that they should be able to receive five dimes of silver for each hour. They are not necessarily completely "fulfilling their obligations," because the school does solve their living problems such as "food" and "lodging" after all. At least they have the benefit of "being able to live in a hotel without paying," which can be said to be "half-obligatory" in nature. Sometimes, unexpectedly, they may even receive five to ten yuan per month for "transportation expenses."

In a slightly larger private middle school, Chinese language teachers can reliably receive five dimes per hour. If you teach Chinese language in a certain grade for six hours per week in such a school, then you can get twelve yuan, which is considered a sum of "cigarette money" that you have earned.

In a slightly more "established" private middle school, Chinese language teachers can get seven to eight dimes per hour. There is one school that I know of that is like this: seventh grade, seven dimes per hour; eighth grade, seven and a half dimes; ninth grade, eight dimes. (This article mainly describes the situation in middle school.) Private middle schools that pay one yuan per hour are very rare in Shanghai. Public junior high schools can generally reach this amount. In short, this is completely different from the situation in some provinces outside of Shanghai, where Chinese language teachers in junior high schools can receive one yuan, or one yuan and twenty-five cents, or one yuan and fifty cents per hour.

Although the treatment is so low, they are required to work twice as hard. Chinese language teachers need more time to grade Chinese language papers than to teach classes. There is not a single Chinese language teacher who does not have a headache when faced with some barely understandable papers. Usually, a Chinese language teacher who is not very experienced can only grade three or four papers in an hour, and those who are more efficient can only grade six or seven papers. However, there are many "lazy" methods in the middle, that is, to grade narrative essays easily, and argumentative essays are the most difficult. It is best for the students to write something very similar (or even exactly the same), such as asking them to write according to the "outline" you give them, or asking them to translate a classical Chinese essay into vernacular Chinese, or write a "short essay" of more than one hundred words, etc. The easiest thing to do is to tell a short story and ask them to write it down, or to present a short text from the textbook and ask them to delete the sentences that can be omitted to shorten the text. Grading twelve or thirteen or even fifteen or sixteen papers like this only takes you an hour. I remember once at a banquet hosted by the Beixin Bookstore to promote its "Mixed Mandarin" and "Beixin Anthology" for Chinese language teachers in middle schools in this city, a very healthy teacher said that he could grade fifteen or sixteen papers in an hour, and I guessed that he might be using this kind of easy method!

Some people may blame such teachers for being irresponsible, but they really have no choice. They are not only too busy, but also too tired. Usually, it is not too much for a Chinese language teacher to teach twenty hours per week. Teaching two classes of Chinese language and also history or geography, they already have three or four hours of classroom teaching every day, which forces them to return home with tired bodies and stare blankly at more than one hundred (fifty or sixty people per class is very common) barely understandable papers, feeling distressed. What's more, a part-time Chinese language teacher teaches even more hours than twenty hours?

Under such circumstances, it is difficult to have time to engage in research work. The content of their lectures has to be pitifully poor. They have to perfunctorily deal with the students, please the students. Such a teacher has to be a "careless" teacher. Is there even any talk of teaching efficiency here?

In order to avoid "misleading children," I never want to be such a teacher again. But society cannot give people better things to do, and the knowledge sold from the university is completely useless to this society, and I have no other "expertise." For the sake of some necessity, even if I don't want to harm people in my heart, how is it possible?

Blacksmith Shop 290

— Cang Yu

About five years ago, I was introduced to this blacksmith shop. Among us, getting a job is seen like a scholar getting an official position.

This is where we work: on the sandy ground, piles of burning coal fires circled by iron plates, blown by the wind from the underground ventilation pipes, the fire burns very fiercely, and the temperature rises to an extremely high degree. At the same time, the black coal ash and yellow coal smoke also fly up together. Because there is a roof on top and walls on both sides, the air in this room is completely shrouded and occupied by this smoke and ash. When I first came to work here, it was really unbearable, because of the invasion of ash and smoke, my eyes were forced to shed tears all day long, and my nasal cavity and lungs were stimulated by strange smells, and my breathing was simply abnormal. But now I seem to be used to it and don't feel it. When it rains, the ash and smoke cannot get out, which makes it even more uncomfortable. Especially in the summer, with twenty or so piles of fierce coal fires burning, if people are not used to it, they will either die from the heat or suffocate.

Like workers in other departments, we start work at seven o'clock. We are in groups of two or three, each group occupying a pile of coal fire and an iron stool. We first pile the crushed coal tightly, and then chisel open a few holes to let the wind blow out, so that the fire can burn fiercely. Then we bury the wrought iron of the thing we want to make into the coal fire, clamp it with large tongs, and wait until it is burned to a certain color. Then we open the pile of coal, and at this time, the heat and strange smell rush out together. Then we pour cold water on it, and the ash and smoke fly up immediately. But we have to clamp the red-hot iron onto the iron stool without the slightest delay, and beat it with hammers, ding ding dang dang, you one hammer, I one hammer. After beating it, we let it cool, and then put it back in to burn, and then hammer it again after burning.

Overseas Correspondence Network

Reno, the Happy City of Divorce 291

— Mori-kun

This is an interesting story of a capitalist society. Reno, the capital of the state of Nevada in the United States, is geographically just a small metropolis in the barren western mountains, but it is a world-famous divorce city, just as Monaco is a world-famous gambling country.

Judge Stremmel, who allowed 20,000 divorce applications in the Reno divorce court in twelve years, said when he retired at the age of sixty-three: "Two-thirds of marriages are failed surgeries, only divorce."

"Come to Reno for a divorce, and restore the happiness of your marriage!"

In the United States, the laws of the forty-eight states are different. Some states believe that "what God has joined together, let no one separate," and South Carolina absolutely does not allow divorce; in the District of Columbia, divorce is only allowed in cases of adultery. Most states consider serious crimes, abandonment, and abuse as grounds for divorce, and there is a necessary "residence period" for applying for divorce, which must be resided in a certain place for one to three years. But in the state of Nevada, divorce procedures are extremely simple.

What makes the state of Nevada famous is not the snow of the Sierra Nevada (Spanish for "snowy mountains"), not the primeval forests, not the mining industry, but the convenient and rapid divorce law. Reno, together with Paris and Mexico City, is known as the three major divorce capitals of the world. At the same time, Reno is now also famous for gambling.

About seventy years ago, many people came to Reno for the mining industry, and after residing there for six months, they obtained full citizenship.

According to Nevada's divorce law, if divorce is applied for on the grounds of abandonment, failure to raise, or abuse, and there is no appeal, then a unilateral divorce is allowed; and remarriage is allowed immediately after divorce. Since everything in the United States likes to be quick, this is not without reason. Those who want a divorce all run to Reno. As long as they live there for six months, they can be blessed by local laws.

The special prosperity of this matter began about eleven or twelve years ago. Most of the divorce visitors are from the wealthy class, and there are always more than a thousand people every year, consuming two million dollars in gold and silver for this purpose. In this small place, this is really a considerable income.

Because most of the wealthy class come here to travel and divorce, the prosperity of gambling and dancing is also natural, but therefore, even more people come.

Later, the necessary residence period for divorce was reduced from six months to three months, so the number of visitors increased even more.

Now, comparing the numbers of foreign divorces before and after the reduction of the residence period, you can get a general idea:

Before the reduction: 1925—806 cases

After the reduction: 1927—1,603 cases

The economy of the entire United States is in recession, and the mining and railway industries are in decline. Many unemployed people in Reno have switched to the hotel industry, and business is very good.

Since May 1, 1931, the three-month residence period has been changed to six weeks. As a result, the unemployed people in the neighboring states of Oregon and Idaho have come to Reno to share in the waste of the wealthy.

Top-quality wine and top-quality singing and dancing always come to Reno. During the annual Independence Day (July 4), a large boxing match is also held. Recently, there have been 189 divorce cases every day in Reno, and each divorce case is completed in six to ten minutes.

Lawyers can earn one million yuan a year, the court earns 260,000 yuan a year, and public gambling houses earn one million yuan a week, or 52 million yuan a year.

Because remarriage is allowed immediately after divorce, many locals have become rich as a result. A small grocery store owner has become the match of a millionaire woman, and a flower girl can also hook up with a celebrity.

There is also a small thing that is worth mentioning, that is, many wealthy people often throw their wedding rings into the Truckee River in Reno, and some unemployed people and vagrants go to the river at night to pan for rings to exchange for food.

Page 21

This is repeated over and over again. We are full of coal ash and coal dust, our arms are sore, our hands are pinched sore, and we are sweating enough. Only after such tempering does the thing to be made become a rough shape. Sometimes when we encounter making large things, we can use the large steam-powered iron hammer to beat it, which is relatively less labor-intensive. It can be said that we completely hammer these things out by hand, because the foreman only gives us a piece of wrought iron and a pattern. Sometimes we also do the work of bending iron pipes. We take the part of the iron pipe to be bent to burn, burn it red, and then put it between two iron bars and bend it according to the drawing.

In addition to the eight and a half hours of work during the day, we also have to do night work. But not doing night work is something we absolutely don't want to do. Think about it, what can we do with seven or eight dimes of wages a day? Not doing night work would not even be able to support our families! The lower the job, the smaller the wage; the smaller the wage, the more we hope to do more night work. In short, we are desperately fighting with life!

The iron hammer is beating day after day, and the calendar pages are flying by page after page. Five years have passed quickly. During this period, I think we have hammered out a lot of things. They always create some happiness for people and earn profits for some people; but what about us? We are still auctioning off our labor by "sore arms," "pinched hands," and "sweating enough"! Moreover, some partners have been added to this blacksmith shop, and a few more piles of coal fires have been surrounded. The sound of the iron hammer is louder than before, and the coal ash and coal smoke are denser than before.

Short Monograph

Conflicts Between England and Japan in Trade 292

— Xueyou

Anyone paying attention to recent international news would not overlook the recent skirmishes in the trade war between England and Japan, and the complete failure of Anglo-Japanese negotiations! Here, we will try to briefly describe the beginning and end of this Anglo-Japanese trade war.

Since Japan abandoned the gold standard in 1931, it has been actively expanding its trade to the world by taking advantage of the "decline in the value of the yen." As a result, the value of export trade in 1932 increased by 263 million yuan compared to the previous year, reaching a total of 1.41 billion yuan. In 1933, it made even greater strides, increasing by another 451 million yuan compared to 1932, reaching a total of 1.861 billion yuan. This made the British Empire, which claimed the top spot in world trade, unable to help but feel envious.

It wouldn't matter so much if Japan's trade volume was simply increasing gradually. Unfortunately, a quarter of Japan's exports are specifically sold to England itself and its dominions and colonies. In other words, in 1933, Japanese goods exported to the British Empire reached 484 million yen. Among them, goods exported to India were the most numerous, reaching 205 million yen, almost accounting for half of the entire British Empire's imports from Japan.

Even more unfortunately, England has always been the world's leading power in cotton textiles, and has always used cotton textiles as the main export to its dominions and colonies. Japan has just caught up with England, and the goods it exports to British dominions and colonies are also centered on cotton textiles. In terms of cotton textiles alone, in 1933, the total amount exported from Japan to various British territories reached 149 million yuan (877.7 million square yards). India had the most, reaching 71.1 million yen (451.1 million square yards).

During the same period, England exported 485 million square yards of cotton textiles to India. This is almost equal to Japan's export volume to India.

In order to protect its own cotton textile industry and consolidate the power of the British economic bloc, England had no choice but to devise ways to resist Japan's fierce attacks. In August 1932, the British government incited the Indian government to revise the import tariffs on cotton textiles. As a result, Japanese cotton textiles were subject to a heavy tax increase from 31 percent to 50 percent, while the import tax on British cotton textiles remained at 25 percent. In April 1933, British Foreign Secretary Simon also notified Japanese Ambassador to England Matsudaira that the Indo-Japanese commercial treaty concluded in 1904 would be abolished the following year. On September 25, representatives from both Japan and India gathered in Shimla, India, for a meeting that lasted half a month, but ultimately yielded no results. Later, on October 23, the meeting was moved to Delhi. After much consultation, an agreement was finally reached on January 5 of this year. According to this agreement, Japan's annual exports of cotton textiles to India shall not exceed 400 million square yards, and Japan shall purchase 1.5 million bales of raw cotton from India each year. The import tax on Japanese cotton textiles remains at 50 percent.

Now that the trade dispute between Japan and India has been resolved, they will take a step further to negotiate the trade issue between Japan and the British Empire. On February 14 of this year, the Anglo-Japanese private cotton industry conference opened in London. The representatives attending from both sides were all leading figures in their respective countries' cotton industries. After a month of negotiations, they finally broke down due to the issue of regional application (England advocated that the scope of the agreement should include markets in third countries other than England and Japan, while Japan insisted that it should be limited to England itself and its colonies). After the breakdown of the private conference, the entire issue was transferred to the governments of the two countries for resolution. After much back-and-forth consultation, they finally could not reach an agreement. On the 3rd of this month, British Minister of Commerce Runciman handed a memorandum to Japanese Ambassador to England Matsudaira, and thus the consultations between the governments of the two countries also broke down.

Now that the negotiations between the British and Japanese governments have broken down, the British government has mobilized all dominions and colonies to cooperate in rejecting Japanese goods. The Anglo-Japanese trade war has officially begun. (Recently, Australian Foreign Minister Latham went to Japan to hold preliminary trade negotiations with Foreign Minister Hirota. Although there are no official results yet, due to Australia's relationship as a British dominion, it is feared that there will be no satisfactory outcome in the future.) Although the Conservative Party of England (the most powerful force in the current cabinet) is still dreaming of the "Anglo-Japanese Alliance," the reality is already clear: the British cotton textile industry can no longer endure Japan's attacks, and from now on, they can only engage in hand-to-hand combat in the trade war.

Regarding England's military deployment in Singapore and various parts of Southeast Asia, the origins of the Anglo-Dutch secret meeting, and England's attitude in the midst of Japan's opposition to "international aid to China"...we can only grasp the true meaning from the fact of this conflict between England and Japan in trade.

Amateur Learning

Self-Study of Literature - A Few Basic Questions! 293

— Chu

(1) How to Find a Starting Point for Research

Although the starting point of our research is the currently active and concrete literary movement, and the scope is roughly limited to existing Chinese creations and translations, it is a relatively narrow field. But how should beginners find a starting point for research? This is a pressing question.

Studying literature from the perspective of literary history, and then exploring the various branches in order according to the evolution of literature, is a research method from vertical to horizontal, and is a good method for self-study. But here, we have many difficulties: because what we are currently dealing with is literature that is constantly changing, and is a complex, contradictory, and mixed synthesis. There is a lack of systematic opinions and decisions on this phenomenon, like the relatively fixed opinions of past literary history. And the path to self-study that we want to find still requires us to look for living historical materials, to be diligent in exploring news about the organization and actions of the literary world, to collect papers, miscellaneous works, criticisms, anecdotes, and other historical materials about the literary world from the publishing industry and various literary and non-literary publications, and to enrich our own views. From these materials, you can see the mainstream and trends of literary activities. You can have a more accurate understanding of the current complex phenomena and not lose your way forward. Of course, the path that unfolds before you still needs to be determined by your own will.

(2) How to Increase the Ability to Discern

In order to have a considerable ability to understand modern works, you should have knowledge of literary theory. To understand a certain school of works, it is best to first read all the literary theories about that school. Although theory is deduced from facts, a scientific action takes the knowledge accumulated from past actions as the starting point of the theory. Therefore, scientific action is guided by theory.

We should have the following basic knowledge:

1. On Art Theory

2. On Literary Trends

3. On the Social Basis of Literature

4. On Aesthetics... and other more specialized research

This part of the research should account for a significant proportion and is the central point of literary research. From this, you can complete the tasks that should be fulfilled in the first item.

For the above aspects, it can naturally be used as a separate and specialized study.

Only when this part of the work is done sufficiently can you exert your power.

(3) Literature and Other Sciences

Literature is not an isolated thing that is unrelated to other sciences. On the contrary, it maintains appropriate and coordinated connections with social sciences and other sciences. If you want to study literary theory, you need to have a thicker foundation in social sciences and other sciences. A person who lacks research in social sciences cannot truly understand literature or be a literary scholar.

Should a writer and a reader alike deeply plant their own foundation and apply what they have learned to literature?

You must quickly learn the following sciences:

1. Basic knowledge of economics to understand modern society;

2. Basic knowledge of sociology to understand the course of social evolution;

3. Basic knowledge of social ideology to understand social consciousness;

4. Basic knowledge of philosophy on the themes of scientific worldview, worldview, and outlook on life.

(4) Literature and Life

Literature cannot be separated from life. To understand a modern work, even if you have the above theories, if you are detached from practical life, you cannot grasp the center of gravity of the times, and there is a danger of becoming mechanistic or metaphysical. Therefore, a writer and a reader alike should understand literature in practical life.

The Original Broadcast Station of International Broadcasting: Soviet Union's Flax and Ramie Farming 294

During the First Five-Year Plan, the area of flax cultivated land approximately doubled, expanding by 2.7 times compared to before the Great War. At the same time, in other European countries, this area was reduced by more than half (60 percent). In 1932, the Soviet Union's flax production accounted for 90 percent of the total global production.

The large increase in the area of flax fields is based on the social and economic changes in Soviet agriculture.

As for the area of ramie cultivated land, it has now increased to 800,000 hectares (Hectares, a French land area measurement unit), while before the Great War it was only 680,000 hectares.

At the beginning of the First Five-Year Plan, the main producers of flax and ramie were individual farmers (Individual Peasants). At that time (1928), the output of flax and ramie from collective farms only accounted for six thousandths of the total output. By 1932, collective farms and state-owned farms had become the main producers of flax and ramie, and their output had reached more than 65 percent of the total output.

What is particularly needed in the planting of flax and ramie are cultivation machine stations. In 1932, there were 261 such cultivation machine stations specifically designed for planting flax and ramie. There were 7,593 cultivation machines operating on 500,000 hectares of flax cultivated land (one times that of the remaining European countries) and 80,000 hectares of ramie cultivated land.

These many cultivation machine stations are all equipped with the most modern agricultural machinery. Here, there are the best-trained political supervisors, managers, and rural economic forces丨丨these are all powerful tools to greatly increase flax and ramie production.

State-owned farms and collective farms (mostly located in areas with cultivation machine stations) now have 15,000 well-trained flax processing workers.

The results obtained from the efforts to increase flax production are not only that the area of flax cultivated land has expanded, but also that there has been a significant increase in harvests, and the number of flax products that can be sent to the market has naturally increased even more.

The method of purchasing flax is now completely different from before. In the case of unstable market transaction prices, the state needs to stipulate in the contract that it will provide producers (collective or individual) with loan precedents, and the latter will supply cotton products to the state. In these contracts, the state provides producers with necessary production subsidies, such as supplying them with agricultural machinery, mineral fertilizers, grains, selected seeds, and credit and monetary advances. At the same time, flax producers engage in cultivating a certain amount of flax fields, and depending on the agricultural technical consumption required for this cultivation, they are required to contribute a certain percentage of the fine-quality harvest to the state within a certain period of time.

This loan contract for flax began to be piloted in 1927, and the one for ramie began to be piloted in 1929. During this period, this method was only piloted on 9 percent to 14 percent of the cultivated land area. By 1931 and 1932, the area cultivated using this method had increased to more than 84 percent of the total flax field area.

Regarding the collection of flax and ramie, the Soviet government has a special flax industry department to manage it. Here, they constantly plan how to increase production and improve quality.

The task assigned to flax and ramie producers in the First Five-Year Plan was to greatly expand the area of flax cultivated land, and this has developed exactly as desired. The 2.3 million hectares of flax fields and 860,000 hectares of ramie fields stipulated in the 1933 plan were realized without difficulty. Flax production increased by 20 percent in 1933, that is, the total output in one year was 550,000 tons.

Page 23

After you understand the living environment of the upper social strata, you should also understand the lives of strata different from yours. Because of the differences in strata, there are obvious differences in inner consciousness; that is, in daily living habits, living styles, language, etc., different imprints are also left. How should you explore this? This is a very important and interesting question.

On the one hand, you must be loyal to your own life's investigation, meticulously record the truth, and clearly discern the characteristics of your own life stratum. Don't let go of any details. At the same time, you should talk to and mingle with people from different strata of life, and carefully understand everything about them. You should visit factories, mines, warships, schools, offices, slums, and even brothels and prisons. You should pay attention to the tragedies and comedies of life in various social strata. In the streets, trams, and theaters, you should patiently read court judgments, social news, and local communications.

All of these can provide you with rich materials and broaden your horizons.

The above is the most precious learning of life, not just for the study of literature.

Amateur Cafe

Innocent Children: The Greatest Envoys of the Kingdom of Heaven 295

— Wang John

Children are great, so philosophers and poets throughout the ages have worshiped children.

Mencius said: "A great man does not lose the heart of a child." Jesus said: "Children are the greatest envoys of the kingdom of heaven." Lao Tzu said: "Concentrate on weakness like an infant." Goethe even said: "We should take them (children) as teachers." The great thinker Marx also often said: "The place in the Christian Bible that I pay the most attention to is its great friendship for children."

Why are children so worthy of worship? Is the worship of children just a momentary whim of adults? Or do adults really discover in children a greatness that adults do not have? Is the physical strength of children better than that of adults? Is the intelligence of children better than that of adults? Is the experience and thought of children better than that of adults?

To understand the true greatness of children, we cannot measure children with the views of ordinary people. We must experience the greatness of children from the children themselves. American child psychologist Hall said: "Childhood is the paradise of mankind, and adult life is a fall from this." This is absolutely correct. All the wisdom we adults have is inseparable from the prejudices of slaves. All my habits and all the traditions of the past oppress the minds of living people like nightmares. Adults, from childhood to death, do not escape the yoke of slaves. What qualifications do we have to comment on the personality of children?

Children, why are they great? It is because children have the innocence that adults do not have. Children cry when they want to cry, and laugh when they want to laugh. They never care about forces outside of themselves. The nature of children makes children only seek self-development and the satisfaction of happiness. A child is a fearless pursuer of happiness. Children can seek comfort from adults, but the things in their hands cannot be easily given to others. In other words, children are completely natural people who live for themselves. Children have absolutely no prejudices and moral concepts of adults. This is the greatness of children.

Some people may retort: If what you say is true, children are just selfish and self-interested creatures, what greatness is there to speak of, and what is there to worship? My answer is: Yes; children are indeed selfish and self-interested creatures, but this is precisely where the greatness of children lies.

What is greatness? Greatness refers to things that benefit mankind. The reason why children are great is because children are symbols of happiness.

Everyone lives for themselves, and everyone has the instinct to pursue happiness. And when he encounters obstacles in his pursuit of happiness, he can break through the obstacles without any hesitation. The destruction of objects that obstruct him by a child is a manifestation of this instinct. Therefore, many people say that if children had the strength of adults, they would be the greatest murderers in the world.

But we adults all come from children. How do adults lose the nature of childhood? This cannot but be attributed to the social system of mankind. In the long-term struggle for survival, mankind realized that it was necessary to sacrifice certain pleasures and development, and thus a social system that deviated from individual wishes naturally emerged. The social system is to the individual what the owner of a garden is to flowers and trees. The owner always tries to make the flowers and trees lose their self-wishes and development, so that they suit his own preferences. As a result, the social system deprives people of their absolute existence, making people no longer aware of themselves. Later, society not only makes its members sacrifice certain instinctive demands to satisfy certain instinctive demands, but also makes some people sacrifice instinctive demands to satisfy the unlimited demands of other people. At this point, mankind, as Rousseau said:

"Except for the whole and public life, they do not know that they have themselves."

But the needs, instincts, and desires of mankind to seek satisfaction will not be eradicated by suppression. Mankind is like an upward-growing willow. If you force it to bend, you can do it for a while, but its original nature will not change, and it will still flourish upward when artificial forces are out of reach. Therefore, Gaozi said: "Taking nature as benevolence and righteousness is like making a cup from a willow." If mankind cannot completely lose the instinct to seek satisfaction and freedom, children preserve the simple form of these instincts even more. Therefore, children become symbols of happy mankind and are envoys of the kingdom of heaven. The innocence of children awakens the slaves and adults who lost their instincts and desires at the entrance of civilization. Therefore, adults who feel like slaves respect this great enlightenment of children.

Book and Newspaper Recommendations

Two Fairy Tales for Children to Read 296

— Jinshan

The fairy tales that Chinese children read are mostly about princes, young masters, fairies, monsters...and other such characters. The influence of these fairy tales on children, apart from making them fantasize that they can also be in the same situation as the protagonists in the fairy tales, it is very difficult to find some fairy tales that instill social and scientific knowledge in children. But the few fairy tales I have seen now, although they were not written by Chinese people, but were translated, have fulfilled the above requirements and are suitable for Chinese children. So I am now making a brief introduction, which can also be regarded as doing a voluntary advertisement for the bookstore owner.

The first book is "Chaplin's Wanderings" written by the American new writer Colt. The story is about a little boy, Joe, and his two older brothers, Adam and Andy, who went on a picnic one day, but he himself was sick in bed because he ate too much ice cream. He asked to hold a race, but his mother said that the room was too small and could not be held, and asked him to have a good sleep, so he quarreled. But he couldn't resist the power of the sleepy devil, and slowly fell asleep. Then the clown Chaplin appeared. Chaplin carefully arranged a race for Joe; he took Joe to the mayor of New York to ask for a race permit, but the mayor said that the race was too troublesome for him and refused to issue it. Chaplin took Joe to ride an elephant to find the giant Jim 丨丨he was a very kind black man who could play the "Saxophone" (a kind of American musical instrument). The giant Jim kindly agreed to Joe's request, climbed onto the elephant, and began to play his "Saxophone." Everyone who heard him play the "Saxophone" would follow him, and gradually formed a huge race. Joe was very happy in his heart. When they arrived in New York, the mayor and his police had already taken their batons and prepared to arrest them for disturbing the peace. Chaplin escaped, and Joe escaped too. The mayor chased after Joe, and Joe was so scared that he was about to cry, and woke up.

You see, isn't this an interesting fairy tale?

Another book is "The Adventures of Little Trafta" written by Soviet Russian Lozanov, which gives children more novel revelations about society and science.

The story is of course also about a little boy, Trafta. Once, he and his father went out to be guests. But unfortunately, at the train station, the father and son were separated. So Trafta decided to be independent and start living his own life. In this way, in this book, the author tells each reader about the telegraph, the train station management system, the locomotive of the train, the signal machine, the telephone, the car, the postal telephone, the public taxi, the newspaper office, the typesetting, the page layout, the printing, the tram, the inquiry office... and also implies the socialist construction to the readers. The ending is of course that Trafta was found back by his father and mother.

These two books are accompanied by very moving illustrations. The former is 20 cents per volume, and the latter is 50 cents per volume.

Biography of a Famous Person

Marconi, Inventor of Wireless Radio (7) 298

— Sen Ran

We know that since the Renaissance, with the development of capitalism, there have already been many great inventions in science. Leaving aside everything else, just considering the inventions directly related to wireless radio, there were many even before Marconi became famous, such as the electromagnetic telegraph, the generator, the telephone, and wired telegraphy... all of which were invented before Marconi began his research. All these inventions, all the scientific and cultural heritage since the Renaissance, were the foundation for Marconi's invention of wireless radio. Without this foundation, no matter how intelligent or persistent he was, he would not have achieved such success. Imagine, if Marconi had been born in the dark ages of the Middle Ages, could he have invented wireless radio? Of course not! That's one point.

Secondly, the era in which Marconi lived was precisely the era of capitalism's development into imperialism. In this era, the capitalist economic network had already enveloped the entire world. Imperialist countries were vigorously competing for markets to sell goods, and frantically fighting for colonies. Under these circumstances, the rapid transmission of information was required for commerce, military affairs, and politics. Marconi's invention of wireless radio was realized under this demand. Here, we can say that the British naval exercises at that time, the South African War, and Marconi's success were closely related.

At the same time, the place where Marconi was born was also inseparable from his invention. We know that he was born in Italy and active in countries like Britain and the United States. These countries were all advanced countries, and their cultural level was above average. So-called modern civilization was represented by them. Only in such a social environment was it possible for Marconi to invent wireless radio. If he had been born in China or India, he would not have accomplished such a great undertaking.

In addition, Marconi's personal living environment was also very important. The issue is very clear: if he had not been born into a wealthy family, had not received a higher education, and furthermore, if he had not received guidance from Professor Righi, had not received hints from Dr. Hertz's experiments, and had not encountered the help of Preece, then I dare say that no matter how great a genius he was, he would eventually have been buried. As for the invention of wireless radio, that would have been left to others.

Of course, we cannot deny Marconi's intelligence and perseverance. But these are only factors that made it possible for him to become a great inventor. It was the era, society, and his personal living environment that made this possibility a reality.

Finally, after evaluating Marconi, I hope that those who generally worship heroes and geniuses will not be superstitious about heroes and geniuses, and should understand them scientifically. Only in this way will we not fall into a mystical path! (The End)
